## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (single-species growth ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P(t), which is the standard setup for single-species demographic growth models. With only t and P available, classical structures express density-independent growth, density dependence (carrying capacity), Allee effects at low density, harvesting/mortality terms, and time-varying (e.g., seasonal) growth rates.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Constant net influx/outflux: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (immigration/emigration independent of P)
- Linear per-capita density dependence: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * P) (per-capita rate changes linearly with density)
- Verhulst logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying-capacity type saturation via quadratic damping)
- Theta-logistic (generalized logistic) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) (flexible strength/shape of density dependence)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (decelerating growth with log-distance to an upper scale)
- Richards-type growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) ** c3 (extra shape parameter for asymmetric approach to saturation)
- Allee effect (strong) with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth below an Allee threshold, saturation at high P)
- Allee effect (weak) via cubic density term: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * P - c2 * P ** 2) (hump-shaped per-capita growth vs P)
- Harvesting proportional to population: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (constant per-capita removal/mortality on top of density dependence)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed removal independent of P)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment modulates per-capita growth)
- Time-trending growth conditions: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P - c2 * P ** 2 (slow drift in growth with density dependence)
- Pulse-like shock/mortality (smooth): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * exp(-c3 * (t - c4) ** 2) * P (transient event reducing population)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Factorizing out P (i.e., dP_dt = P * g(t, P)) corresponds to modeling per-capita growth rate g; look for g crossing 0 at equilibrium densities.
- A quadratic negative term in P (e.g., -c * P**2) indicates crowding/competition; it creates a stable upper equilibrium where dP_dt = 0.
- Multiple real roots in dP_dt as a function of P (e.g., P*(P-c1)*(1-c2*P)) indicate multiple equilibria; the smallest positive root often represents an Allee threshold.
- A log term log(c/P) typically implies Gompertz-type regulation where proportional growth slows roughly with log-distance to an upper scale, often fitting sigmoidal trajectories with asymmetric approach.
- Periodic dependence on t (sin/cos) in the coefficient of P suggests seasonal forcing; expect oscillations in instantaneous growth rate even if P changes smoothly.
- Subtracting a constant term (e.g., -c2) represents fixed-yield removal; it can create extinction thresholds because losses do not vanish as P decreases.
- Subtracting a term proportional to P (e.g., -c2*P) represents additional mortality; it shifts the effective growth rate without changing the basic density-dependence shape.
- Gaussian-in-time modifiers exp(-c*(t-c0)**2) capture transient shocks (disease, disasters) localized around a time; these appear as temporary dips in dP_dt.
- Allowing coefficients to vary with t (e.g., c0 + c1*t) encodes gradual environmental change; it can move equilibria over time (non-autonomous dynamics).

P appears only as the single input variable, entering as P^{1/3}, P, inside sin(·) via its phase, and inside log(·) via a small slope 0.08682. Given the fitted values, the sinusoidal contribution is effectively negligible (amplitude ≈2×10^{-3}) compared with the linear and log terms, while the large negative log scale makes the log term a major nonlinear correction; for small-to-moderate P, log(1+0.08682P)≈0.08682P so this contributes an approximately linear subtraction ≈−3.31P, partly canceling the +2.54P term. Thus the formula is approximately 0.7686·P^{1/3}+2.5437·P−38.12·log(1+0.08682·P) (with a tiny oscillatory residual), consistent with the near-zero NMSE.

= `-1 + P/14.33285523805181 + P/8.670374869520632 - P²/(8.670374869520632 * 14.33285523805181)`
= `-1 + P*(1/14.33285523805181 + 1/8.670374869520632) - P²/124.268...`

So GT = `c0 * [-1 + P*A - P²*B] * P + c5 * P^(1/3)`
= `c0 * [-P + A*P² - B*P³] + c5 * P^(1/3)`

**GT simplified form:** `α*P^(1/3) + β*P + γ*P² + δ*P³`

where:
- α = 0.768873878858443 (coefficient of P^(1/3))
- β = -0.768873878858443 (coefficient of P)
- γ = 0.768873878858443 * (1/14.332855... + 1/8.670374...) (coefficient of P²)
- δ = -0.768873878858443 / (8.670374... * 14.332855...) (coefficient of P³)

So GT is: **c₀*P^(1/3) + c₁*P + c₂*P² + c₃*P³**

This is a sum of four basis functions: P^(1/3), P, P², P³.

Now let me check each candidate:

**Candidate 1:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + c2*sin(P*c3 + c4) + c5*log(P*c6 + 1)`
Has sin and log terms that can't be zeroed without losing P and P^(1/3) terms. Setting c2=0 and c5=0 leaves only P^(1/3) and P, missing P² and P³.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `P*P^c0*c1 + P*c2 + P^c0*c3 + c4*sin(c5*log(c6*|P|+1)+c7)`
Setting c4=0 eliminates sin. Then: c1*P^(1+c0) + c2*P + c3*P^c0. If c0=1/3: c1*P^(4/3) + c2*P + c3*P^(1/3). Missing P² and P³.
If c0=2: c1*P³ + c2*P + c3*P². Then missing P^(1/3). Can't get all four basis functions.
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `P^(3/2)*c0 + √P*c1 + P*c2 + c3 + c4*cos(P*c5+c6)`

This is exactly P^(1/3) + P + P² + P³. ✓
